The company was acquired by Henry Schein, Inc. in October 2006 and now operates as a subsidiary of Henry Schein Medical Systems, Inc. Henry Schein is a Fortune 500 healthcare distribution company (publicly traded on NASDAQ: HSIC). MicroMD develops practice management, electronic medical records, document management, and patient engagement software for independent medical practices and community health centers across the United States.\n     9→\n    10→MicroMD targets small-to-medium independent practices, multi-specialty groups, community health centers (CHCs), Federally Qualified Health Centers (FQHCs), and Rural Health Centers (RHCs). The company claims a 12-year average customer retention rate and 98% support satisfaction rating. They were recognized in the 2017 KLAS Awards as Best Ambulatory EMR/PM. MicroMD supports eight named specialties: Cardiology, Dermatology, ENT, Gastroenterology, Ob-Gyn, Pediatrics, Primary Care, and Urology. The product is available as client-server (on-premise) or web-based ASP (cloud) deployment.\n    11→\n    12→The CHPL listing names the developer as \"MicroMD, LLC\" but press releases and investor relations materials consistently refer to \"Henry Schein Medical Systems\" as the certifying entity. It is part of a broader MicroMD product suite that includes separate but tightly integrated modules for Practice Management (PM), Document Management (DMS), electronic prescribing (e-Rx), and the Secure Chart patient portal. The certified EMR module is one component of a larger product ecosystem — the practice management, document management, and patient portal modules are separate products that share data through integration interfaces.\n    21→\n    22→The EMR is certified for a broad range of criteria: clinical data capture (a)(1)–(a)(5), (a)(12), (a)(14)–(a)(15); transitions of care (b)(1)–(b)(3); clinical quality measures (c)(1)–(c)(3); public health reporting (f)(1)–(f)(2), (f)(4); FHIR APIs (g)(7), (g)(10); and the EHI export criterion (b)(10). Patients interact through the Secure Chart patient portal.\n    33→\n    34→The vendor distributes through Henry Schein's sales network. No specific customer count was found on the website, but the 12-year average retention and KLAS recognition suggest a stable installed base. Pricing starts at approximately $200/month per user (per third-party reviews), suggesting a mid-market positioning.\n    35→\n    36→### Modules & Functionality\n    37→\n    38→**Clinical syndromic surveillance\n   116→\n   117→### Data & Content\n   118→\n   119→Based on the features and modules described above, MicroMD EMR and its integrated product suite manage the following data:\n   120→\n   121→**Clinical data (EMR)**: Patient demographics, encounter notes (SOAP format), problem lists, medication lists, allergy lists, immunization records, vital signs, clinical images and annotated anatomical diagrams, lab orders and results, medical device data (ECGs, spirometry, Holter), health maintenance records, clinical alerts, referral information, ICD-10 diagnoses, care plans, and clinical quality measure data.\n   122→\n   123→**Prescribing data**: Medication orders, prescription history, controlled substance prescriptions (EPCS), drug interaction alerts, pharmacy routing information (via Surescripts).\n   124→\n   125→**Practice management data (PM module)**: Appointment schedules, patient registration and demographic data, insurance information and eligibility history, claims and billing records, payment history (remittance, patient payments), accounts receivable data, fee schedules (including sliding fee for FQHCs), provider staffing and utilization data.\n   126→\n   127→**Document management data (DMS module)**: Scanned documents, e-faxes, pathology results, correspondence, staff and vendor records, intake forms, Microsoft Word templates.\n   128→\n   129→**Patient portal data (Secure Chart)**: Secure messages between patients and practice, appointment requests, patient-entered intake forms, published lab results and documents.\n   130→\n   131→**Public health data**: Immunization registry submissions, electronic case reports, syndromic surveillance data.\n   132→\n   133→**Important note on product boundaries**: The certified module is \"MicroMD EMR\" but the full product ecosystem includes separate PM, DMS, and Secure Chart modules that share data through integration interfaces. It is unclear from the vendor's materials exactly which data is stored within the EMR module versus the PM, DMS, or portal modules. The PM and EMR share demographic data, insurance information, scheduling details, referrals, and charges. The EHI export requirement under (b)(10) covers \"all electronic health information that can be stored at the time of certification by the product, of which the Health IT Module is a part\" — which would encompass the full product, not just the certified EMR module.\n   134→\n   135→**User reviews on Capterra (3.2/5 from ~20 reviews)** note that reporting capabilities are \"antiquated and cumbersome\" and that the system \"struggles with integrations, lacking the ability to build flat-file transfers.\" Users praise the intuitive interface and tight lab/device integration.\n   136→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. The company was acquired by Henry Schein, Inc. in October 2006 and now operates as a subsidiary of Henry Schein Medical Systems, Inc. Henry Schein is a Fortune 500 healthcare distribution company (publicly traded on NASDAQ: HSIC). MicroMD develops practice management, electronic medical records, document management, and patient engagement software for independent medical practices and community health centers across the United States.\n\nMicroMD targets small-to-medium independent practices, multi-specialty groups, community health centers (CHCs), Federally Qualified Health Centers (FQHCs), and Rural Health Centers (RHCs). The company claims a 12-year average customer retention rate and 98% support satisfaction rating. They were recognized in the 2017 KLAS Awards as Best Ambulatory EMR/PM. MicroMD supports eight named specialties: Cardiology, Dermatology, ENT, Gastroenterology, Ob-Gyn, Pediatrics, Primary Care, and Urology. The product is available as client-server (on-premise) or web-based ASP (cloud) deployment.\n\nThe CHPL listing names the developer as \"MicroMD, LLC\" but press releases and investor relations materials consistently refer to \"Henry Schein Medical Systems\" as the certifying entity. The Drummond Group certifies the product.\n\n## Product: MicroMD EMR\n\nCHPL IDs: 11281\n\n### What It Is\n\nMicroMD EMR is a 2015 Edition CEHRT (Certified EHR Technology) ambulatory electronic medical records system. It is part of a broader MicroMD product suite that includes separate but tightly integrated modules for Practice Management (PM), Document Management (DMS), electronic prescribing (e-Rx), and the Secure Chart patient portal. The certified EMR module is one component of a larger product ecosystem — the practice management, document management, and patient portal modules are separate products that share data through integration interfaces.\n\nThe EMR is certified for a broad range of criteria: clinical data capture (a)(1)–(a)(5), (a)(12), (a)(14)–(a)(15); transitions of care (b)(1)–(b)(3); clinical quality measures (c)(1)–(c)(3); public health reporting (f)(1)–(f)(2), (f)(4); FHIR APIs (g)(7), (g)(10); and the EHI export criterion (b)(10). The SED intended user description is \"Ambulatory.\"\n\n### Users & Market\n\nMicroMD serves independent ambulatory practices ranging from solo providers to larger multi-specialty groups and community health centers. Key user segments include:\n\n- **Independent practices**: Small-to-medium physician offices across multiple specialties\n- **Community health centers**: CHCs, FQHCs, and RHCs with specialized features like sliding fee schedules, UDS reporting, and dental billing\n- **Multi-specialty groups**: Practices across cardiology, dermatology, ENT, gastroenterology, Ob-Gyn, pediatrics, primary care, and urology\n\nDay-to-day users include physicians (clinical documentation, ordering, prescribing), clinical staff (documentation, health maintenance), front office staff (scheduling, registration, eligibility verification), billing staff (claims management, payment posting, collections), and practice managers (reporting, analytics). Patients interact through the Secure Chart patient portal.\n\nThe vendor distributes through Henry Schein's sales network. No specific customer count was found on the website, but the 12-year average retention and KLAS recognition suggest a stable installed base. Pricing starts at approximately $200/month per user (per third-party reviews), suggesting a mid-market positioning.\n\n### Modules & Functionality\n\n**Clinical Documentation (EMR Core)**\n- Multiple documentation methods: SOAP format, free-text entry, templates, forms, and speech recognition (Dragon Premier Partner integration)\n- ICD-10 code search and assignment\n- Image management with anatomical diagram annotation\n- Customizable templates at no additional cost\n- Specialty-specific workflows for eight named specialties\n\n**e-Prescribing**\n- Two-way e-prescribing through Surescripts\n- Controlled substance prescribing via MicroMD EPCS Gold\n- Drug interaction checking and medication safety alerts\n\n**Clinical Decision Support**\n- Health maintenance alerts and reminders\n- Drug interaction and allergy checking\n- Immunization tracking and status display\n- Patient overview dashboard with customizable alerts\n\n**Lab Integration**\n- Interfaces with major labs: LabCorp, Quest Diagnostics, Fletcher-Flora Health Care, 4Medica, Schulyer House\n- Electronic lab ordering and results delivery\n- Demographic data export to labs\n\n**Medical Device Integration**\n- Real-time connectivity with devices from Welch Allyn, Midmark, and Burdick\n- Supports ECGs, Holter monitors, and spirometers\n- Direct data capture from devices into patient records\n\n**Telehealth**\n- Medpod virtual video visit integration (launched with Version 17)\n- HIPAA-secure video visits documented in the EMR\n- Available as pay-per-encounter or annual subscription\n\n**Practice Management (Separate PM Module, Integrated)**\n- Appointment scheduling with intelligent waiting lists\n- Patient registration with OCR scanning of ID/insurance cards\n- Automated eligibility verification with insurance effective date tracking\n- Claims management with EDI processing through clearinghouse partners (ECP, Gateway EDI, RealMed, Practice Insight)\n- Code scrubbing to flag errors before submission\n- Payment posting via electronic remittance, manual entry, or batch processing\n- Patient statements, payment plans, and credit card processing\n- Accounts receivable reporting and RBRVS benchmarking\n- Direct EDI connections with Medicare, Medicaid, and Blues plans\n- Collections account export functionality\n\n**Community Health / FQHC Features**\n- Sliding fee schedule calculations for patients at various income levels\n- UDS reporting for grant compliance\n- ADA dental billing integration (Dentrix compatibility)\n- Temporary patient registration\n\n**Document Management (MicroMD DMS — Separate Module)**\n- Electronic document filing, scanning, and indexing\n- Stores patient account charts, pathology results, labs, and non-patient documents (staff, vendor, correspondence)\n- Drag-and-drop sorting, markup and annotation tools\n- Integration with external documents and e-faxes\n\n**Patient Portal (Secure Chart — Separate Module)**\n- Two-way patient-to-practice secure messaging\n- Online appointment scheduling and requests\n- Lab results and document sharing\n- Digital patient intake forms\n- Appointment reminders via email, text, and voice\n- Post-visit surveys\n- Two-way texting\n\n**Reporting & Analytics**\n- Accounts receivable, claims tracking, financial analysis reports\n- Export to Excel/Access formats with graphical display\n- ODBC-compliant database for third-party reporting (Crystal Reports, etc.)\n- Clinical quality measure reporting for MIPS\n\n**Interoperability**\n- HL7 standard, XML specification, Internet protocols\n- Published Windows APIs for integration\n- FHIR API access (certified for g(7) and g(10))\n- C-CDA document support for transitions of care\n- Public health reporting: immunization registries, electronic case reporting, syndromic surveillance\n\n### Data & Content\n\nBased on the features and modules described above, MicroMD EMR and its integrated product suite manage the following data:\n\n**Clinical data (EMR)**: Patient demographics, encounter notes (SOAP format), problem lists, medication lists, allergy lists, immunization records, vital signs, clinical images and annotated anatomical diagrams, lab orders and results, medical device data (ECGs, spirometry, Holter), health maintenance records, clinical alerts, referral information, ICD-10 diagnoses, care plans, and clinical quality measure data.\n\n**Prescribing data**: Medication orders, prescription history, controlled substance prescriptions (EPCS), drug interaction alerts, pharmacy routing information (via Surescripts).\n\n**Practice management data (PM module)**: Appointment schedules, patient registration and demographic data, insurance information and eligibility history, registry submissions, electronic case reports, syndromic surveillance data.\n\n**Important note on product boundaries**: The certified module is \"MicroMD EMR\" but the full product ecosystem includes {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01S1nT3cdishn3fUxPhPHKF1","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_018FaNDkR7JDFeJMCo8Je8oM","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/home/jmandel/hobby/ehi-export-analysis/results/micromd-llc/ehi-export-report.md","content":"# MicroMD, LLC — EHI Export Documentation\n\nCollected: 2026-02-14\n\n## Source\n- Registered URL: https://www.micromd.com/micromd-emr-certified/\n- CHPL IDs: 11281\n- Product: MicroMD EMR Version 20.0\n- Certification date: 2023-04-27\n\n## Navigation Journal\n\n1. **Initial probe**: `curl -sI -L \"https://www.micromd.com/micromd-emr-certified/\" -H 'User-Agent: Mozilla/5.0'` returned HTTP 200, Content-Type: text/html. WordPress site.\n\n2. **Fetched page**: `curl -sL \"https://www.micromd.com/micromd-emr-certified/\" -H 'User-Agent: Mozilla/5.0' -o /tmp/micromd-page.html` — 130,670 bytes. Static WordPress page with certification information.\n\n3. **Found downloadable files**: Searched HTML for file links. Found one EHI-specific PDF:\n   - `/docs/MicroMD-EMR-170.315b10-Electronic-Health-Information-export-EHI.pdf`\n   - Also found: Real World Test Plans/Results (2022–2025), costs PDF, and a FHIR API documentation link (`https://micromd.dynamicfhir.com/micromd/basepractice/r4/Home/ApiDocumentation` — this is the (g)(10) API, not the (b)(10) export).\n\n4. **Downloaded PDF**: `curl -sL \"https://www.micromd.com/docs/MicroMD-EMR-170.315b10-Electronic-Health-Information-export-EHI.pdf\" -H 'User-Agent: Mozilla/5.0' -o downloads/MicroMD-EMR-170.315b10-Electronic-Health-Information-export-EHI.pdf` — confirmed as PDF document, 17 pages, 326,238 bytes.\n\n5. **Examined page in browser**: Navigated to URL, took screenshot. Page is a single certification information page with the EHI PDF link prominently listed alongside other certification materials. The EHI link text reads \"170.315 (b) (10) Electronic Health Information export (EHI)\" and links directly to the PDF.\n\n6. **Verified no additional content**: The page contains no accordion sections, embedded documentation, or additional EHI-specific content beyond the PDF link. The FHIR API link is a separate (g)(10) concern.\n\n## What Was Found\n\nThe EHI export documentation is a single 17-page PDF dated February 6, 2026 (recently updated), authored by \"Creative Group\" in Microsoft Word. It describes MicroMD EMR's (b)(10) EHI export mechanism and provides a complete XML schema for the export output.\n\n### Export Format\n\nThe export produces a **compressed (ZIP) file** that is:\n- Named with the convention `{practiceId}.{patientChartId}.0`\n- Password-protected using the patient's date of birth (mmddyyyy format)\n- Contains multiple **XML files** following a proprietary schema\n\nThe documentation refers to a \"user manual for instruction\" on how to perform the export, but this user manual is not publicly available on the page.\n\n### XML File Schema\n\nThe export consists of **10 XML files** plus additional DMS (Document Management System) files:\n\n1. **Billing.xml** — Superbills with CPT codes, diagnoses (ICD/SNOMED), procedures, modifiers, referring physicians, and insurance information per transaction.\n\n2. **Encounters.xml** — The most detailed file. Contains encounter metadata plus nested elements for:\n   - Reasons for visit (with SNOMED codes)\n   - Assessments (ICD codes, SNOMED codes, with detail descriptors)\n   - Subjective findings (SOAP S-section)\n   - Objective findings (SOAP O-section)\n   - Review of problems\n   - Medications (with NDC, RxNorm, GCN seq numbers, sig details, multi-sig support)\n   - Plans (orders, lab orders, referrals, vaccinations, procedure codes)\n   - Face time records\n   - Medical info links\n   - Encounter notes (text and audio recordings, graphics)\n\n3. **HealthScreening.xml** — Contains:\n   - Goal monitoring with progress tracking\n   - Health concerns with related concerns, risks, and care teams\n   - Health screenings (questionnaires with questions, answers, follow-ups, results, sections — LOINC-coded)\n   - Immunizations (CVX codes, NDC, VIS sheets, lot numbers, administration details, side effects)\n   - Risk factors\n   - Prevention programs with details and associated programs\n\n4. **Histories.xml** — Family, medical, social, surgical history, plus:\n   - Birth history (Apgar scores, delivery details)\n   - Sexual history\n   - Asthma history (detailed trigger and symptom tracking)\n   - Habit tracking\n   - Hospitalization records (with procedures, diagnoses, reports)\n   - Consent history\n\n5. **MedicalInfo.xml** — Core clinical data:\n   - Allergies (with coded types, severity, reactions)\n   - Problems/conditions (ICD-10, SNOMED codes, with cancer staging data)\n   - Vitals (BP, HR, RR, temp, BMI, O2 sat, pain, head circumference, OB-specific vitals)\n   - Medications (comprehensive: NDC, RxNorm, GCN, dispensing details, refill info)\n   - Test results (LOINC-coded, with normal ranges, abnormal flags)\n   - Behavioral health screenings (questionnaire format)\n   - Clinical decision support alerts, actions, references, recommendations, treatments\n   - Ultrasound/PIMD data (detailed fetal measurements)\n   - Operations (procedures, diagnoses, medications, flow records, personnel)\n   - Treatment plans (objectives, problems, medications, interventions, progress, care teams)\n\n6. **Miscellaneous.xml** — Attachments, letters, advance directives, patient education, referrals in, and transitions of care.\n\n7. **Orders.xml** — Orders with category, priority, sender/receiver, status, and associated work-to-do items.\n\n8. **Patient.xml** — Demographics (including SOGI data, race/ethnicity, multiple addresses), family members, contacts, insurance policies (with detailed plan and policyholder information), providers (practice and referring), and consent records (including CCM consent details).\n\n9. **Schedule.xml** — Appointment records with status, provider, times, department, and specialty.\n\n10. **Specialty.xml** — Specialty-specific data modules:\n    - Vision (detailed ophthalmic tests including acuity, tonometry, confrontation, color vision)\n    - Hearing (audiometric levels, thresholds, reports)\n    - Diabetes (insulin tracking, dose management, pump basal rates)\n    - Pediatric developmental assessments\n    - Genetic screenings with family relationships\n    - Geriatric assessments (questionnaire format)\n    - Allergy testing (skin test results)\n\n11. **WomenHealth.xml** — Obstetric and gynecologic data:\n    - Obstetric care episodes (comprehensive prenatal data)\n    - Initial physical exams\n    - Detailed OB medical history (40+ condition fields)\n    - Genetic screenings\n    - Deliveries (with fetal data, labor events, complications)\n    - Prenatal visits (fundal height, cervical status, fetal monitoring)\n    - Estimated date of delivery calculations\n    - Progress of labor records\n    - Pregnancy history (with fetal outcomes)\n    - Gynecology history\n    - Menstrual history\n    - Family planning\n\n12. **Additional DMS files** — \"Additional files will be included from the document management system. These will have the file name and format as saved in the DMS system. They may include pdf, doc, rtf, ccd, xml, image formats, etc.\"\n\n## Export Coverage Assessment\n\n### Data Domain Coverage\n\nThis is a genuinely comprehensive (b)(10) export that covers data well beyond the USCDI/US Core subset. Comparing against the product research:\n\n**Clearly covered:**\n- Clinical encounters and SOAP documentation\n- Billing/superbill data (CPT codes, diagnoses, modifiers, insurance)\n- Problem lists, medication lists, allergy lists\n- Immunization records (detailed, CVX/NDC coded)\n- Lab/test results (LOINC coded)\n- Vital signs\n- Patient demographics (including SOGI, race/ethnicity)\n- Insurance information (detailed plan data)\n- Family/medical/social/surgical history\n- Health screening questionnaires\n- Clinical decision support alerts\n- Advance directives\n- Patient education records\n- Referrals (in and out via transitions of care)\n- Orders\n- Appointment scheduling\n- Specialty-specific data (vision, hearing, diabetes, pediatric, geriatric, allergy testing)\n- Women's health/OB-GYN (extremely detailed)\n- Attachments and documents (from DMS integration)\n- Care plans/treatment plans with goals and progress\n- Consent records\n- Operations/surgical procedures\n\n**Partially covered or ambiguous:**\n- **Practice management financial data**: Billing.xml includes superbill-level data (CPT codes, insurance references, payment methods), but it's unclear whether full accounts receivable, payment posting, ERA/EOB data, claims adjudication status, and collections data are included. The billing data appears to capture the clinical billing events but may not capture the full financial lifecycle.\n- **Patient portal content**: Secure messages between patient and practice are not explicitly mentioned in the schema. The portal interaction data may not be in the export.\n- **Audit trails**: No explicit audit log or access history export is documented. While individual records have `recordedby` and `recordedon` fields (basic provenance), there's no dedicated audit log export.\n- **E-prescribing transaction logs**: Medications include prescription IDs and pharmacy instructions, but the Surescripts transaction history itself is not explicitly represented.\n\n**Appears missing:**\n- **Full practice management accounting**: Payment posting, ERA processing, patient statement history, collections account data — the PM module data appears absent beyond superbill-level billing.\n- **Document content**: DMS files are included as attachments but the DMS indexing/metadata (filing categories, annotation data) is only partially captured in the Attachment element.\n- **Communication logs**: Patient-practice secure messages, appointment reminders sent, post-visit surveys.\n- **User/provider management data**: Provider credentials, privileges, staff records (beyond what's in encounter contexts).\n\n### Export Format & Standards\n\nThe export uses a **proprietary XML format** — not FHIR, not C-CDA, not any external standard. This is entirely appropriate for a (b)(10) export that needs to capture everything the product stores. Key observations:\n\n- **Well-structured XML**: The schema is hierarchical, with logical grouping of related data (encounters contain their assessments, medications, plans; patients contain their addresses, contacts, insurance).\n- **Standard code systems referenced**: Fields reference ICD-10 (`icdcode`), SNOMED (`snocode`), CPT (`cptcode`), CVX (`cvxcode`), NDC (`ndc`), RxNorm (`rxnorm`), LOINC (`loinc`), and NPI (`npi`). This means the data is coded, not just free text.\n- **Relationships via IDs**: Records are linked via IDs (`patientid`, `encounterid`, `transactionid`, `medicationid`, etc.), allowing reconstruction of relationships.\n- **Per-patient export**: The export is patient-scoped — each export file is for a single patient chart.\n- **Password protection**: The ZIP uses the patient DOB as password, which is a minimal security measure.\n\nA third party could reconstruct the clinical record from this export, though they would need to understand MicroMD's data model to interpret all the fields — many field names are self-explanatory (e.g., `firstname`, `icdcode`, `doseamount`) but some require domain knowledge (e.g., `gcnseqno`, `ADPType`, `bdagetype`).\n\n### Documentation Quality\n\n**Strengths:**\n- The document provides the **complete XML schema** for every export file, listing every element and attribute\n- The hierarchical nesting is clear\n- The format is self-documenting in that most attribute names are descriptive\n- The document is well-organized by file, with each XML file getting its own section\n- Recently updated (February 2026), suggesting active maintenance\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n- **No field-level descriptions**: Attributes are listed but never defined. What does `confidentiality` mean? What values can `billingstatus` take? What's the format of date fields?\n- **No data type specifications**: No indication of which fields are dates, integers, strings, coded values, etc.\n- **No value sets**: Coded fields like `maritalstatus`, `billingstatus`, `encountertype` lack enumeration of valid values\n- **No cardinality**: No indication of which elements can repeat or are required vs. optional\n- **No sample data**: No example export files or records showing what populated data looks like\n- **No import instructions**: A developer receiving this export would have to reverse-engineer the data types and value sets\n- **User manual referenced but not provided**: The document says \"see user manual for instruction\" on how to perform the export, but the manual is not publicly available\n- **No versioning information**: No indication of schema version or change history\n\n### Structure & Completeness\n\nThe documentation operates at the **attribute-name level** — it tells you exactly what fields exist in each XML element, which is more granular than just listing table names, but less granular than a full data dictionary with types, constraints, and descriptions. It is essentially an XML Schema rendered as prose, but without the formal type information that an actual XSD would provide.\n\nThe export is clearly the result of genuine (b)(10) work, not a repackaged (g)(10) FHIR API. It exports the full breadth of MicroMD's data model — billing, specialty workflows, OB/GYN, scheduling, DMS attachments — well beyond what any FHIR US Core API would cover. The proprietary XML format is appropriate for this purpose.\n\nThe critical gap is the lack of field-level documentation. A recipient of this export would know the structure but would need to guess at data types, valid values, and the meaning of ambiguous field names. Adding an actual XSD and a field glossary would significantly improve the documentation.\n\n## Access Summary\n- Final URL (after redirects): https://www.micromd.com/micromd-emr-certified/\n- Status: found\n- Required browser: no\n- Navigation complexity: one_click (single PDF link on certification page)\n- Anti-bot issues: none\n\n## Obstacles & Dead Ends\n- No obstacles encountered. The page loaded cleanly via curl and in the browser.\n- The FHIR API documentation link (`https://micromd.dynamicfhir.com/micromd/basepractice/r4/Home/ApiDocumentation`) was noted but not downloaded — it documents the (g)(10) Standardized API, not the (b)(10) EHI export. The EHI export uses a completely separate proprietary XML format, so the FHIR API docs are irrelevant to the export.\n- The \"user manual for instruction\" on performing the export is referenced in the PDF but not publicly available on the certification page.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":251,"cache_read_input_tokens":81067,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":251},"output_tokens":25,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"716623a8-9a09-419d-9ece-963de7e6f8af","uuid":"c0b9b3ba-8b49-474d-8bab-feff3f65e736"}

Allergies (with coded types, severity, reactions)\n   - Problems/conditions (ICD-10, SNOMED codes, with cancer staging data)\n   - Vitals (BP, HR, RR, temp, BMI, O2 sat, pain, head circumference, OB-specific vitals)\n   - Medications (comprehensive: NDC, RxNorm, GCN, dispensing details, refill info)\n   - Test results (LOINC-coded, with normal ranges, abnormal flags)\n   - Behavioral health screenings (questionnaire format)\n   - Clinical decision support alerts, actions, references, recommendations, treatments\n   - Ultrasound/PIMD data (detailed fetal measurements)\n   - Operations (procedures, diagnoses, medications, flow records, personnel)\n   - Treatment plans (objectives, problems, medications, interventions, progress, care teams)\n\n6. **Miscellaneous.xml** — Attachments, letters, advance directives, patient education, referrals in, and transitions of care.\n\n7. **Orders.xml** — Orders with category, priority, sender/receiver, status, and associated work-to-do items.\n\n8. **Patient.xml** — Demographics (including SOGI data, race/ethnicity, multiple addresses), family members, contacts, insurance policies (with detailed plan and policyholder information), providers (practice and referring), and consent records (including CCM consent details).\n\n9. **Schedule.xml** — Appointment records with status, provider, times, department, and specialty.\n\n10. **Specialty.xml** — Specialty-specific data modules:\n    - Vision (detailed ophthalmic tests including acuity, tonometry, confrontation, color vision)\n    - Hearing (audiometric levels, thresholds, reports)\n    - Diabetes (insulin tracking, dose management, pump basal rates)\n    - Pediatric developmental assessments\n    - Genetic screenings with family relationships\n    - Geriatric assessments (questionnaire format)\n    - Allergy testing (skin test results)\n\n11. **WomenHealth.xml** — Obstetric and gynecologic data:\n    - Obstetric care episodes (comprehensive prenatal data)\n    - Initial physical exams\n    - Detailed OB medical history (40+ condition fields)\n    - Genetic screenings\n    - Deliveries (with fetal data, labor events, complications)\n    - Prenatal visits (fundal height, cervical status, fetal monitoring)\n    - Estimated date of delivery calculations\n    - Progress of labor records\n    - Pregnancy history (with fetal outcomes)\n    - Gynecology history\n    - Menstrual history\n    - Family planning\n\n12. **Additional DMS files** — \"Additional files will be included from the document management system. These will have the file name and format as saved in the DMS system. They may include pdf, doc, rtf, ccd, xml, image formats, etc.\"\n\n## Export Coverage Assessment\n\n### Data Domain Coverage\n\nThis is a genuinely comprehensive (b)(10) export that covers data well beyond the USCDI/US Core subset. Comparing against the product research:\n\n**Clearly covered:**\n- Clinical encounters and SOAP documentation\n- Billing/superbill data (CPT codes, diagnoses, modifiers, insurance)\n- Problem lists, medication lists, allergy lists\n- Immunization records (detailed, CVX/NDC coded)\n- Lab/test results (LOINC coded)\n- Vital signs\n- Patient demographics (including SOGI, race/ethnicity)\n- Insurance information (detailed plan data)\n- Family/medical/social/surgical history\n- Health screening questionnaires\n- Clinical decision support alerts\n- Advance directives\n- Patient education records\n- Referrals (in and out via transitions of care)\n- Orders\n- Appointment scheduling\n- Specialty-specific data (vision, hearing, diabetes, pediatric, geriatric, allergy testing)\n- Women's health/OB-GYN (extremely detailed)\n- Attachments and documents (from DMS integration)\n- Care plans/treatment plans with goals and progress\n- Consent records\n- Operations/surgical procedures\n\n**Partially covered or ambiguous:**\n- **Practice management financial data**: Billing.xml includes superbill-level data (CPT codes, insurance references, payment methods), but it's unclear whether full accounts receivable, payment posting, ERA/EOB data, claims adjudication status, and collections data are included. The billing data appears to capture the clinical billing events but may not capture the full financial lifecycle.\n- **Patient portal content**: Secure messages between patient and practice are not explicitly mentioned in the schema. The portal interaction data may not be in the export.\n- **Audit trails**: No explicit audit log or access history export is documented. While individual records have `recordedby` and `recordedon` fields (basic provenance), there's no dedicated audit log export.\n- **E-prescribing transaction logs**: Medications include prescription IDs and pharmacy instructions, but the Surescripts transaction history itself is not explicitly represented.\n\n**Appears missing:**\n- **Full practice management accounting**: Payment posting, ERA processing, patient statement history, collections account data — the PM module data appears absent beyond superbill-level billing.\n- **Document content**: DMS files are included as attachments but the DMS indexing/metadata (filing categories, annotation data) is only partially captured in the Attachment element.\n- **Communication logs**: Patient-practice secure messages, appointment reminders sent, post-visit surveys.\n- **User/provider management data**: Provider credentials, privileges, staff records (beyond what's in encounter contexts).\n\n### Export Format & Standards\n\nThe export uses a **proprietary XML format** — not FHIR, not C-CDA, not any external standard. This is entirely appropriate for a (b)(10) export that needs to capture everything the product stores. Key observations:\n\n- **Well-structured XML**: The schema is hierarchical, with logical grouping of related data (encounters contain their assessments, medications, plans; patients contain their addresses, contacts, insurance).\n- **Standard code systems referenced**: Fields reference ICD-10 (`icdcode`), SNOMED (`snocode`), CPT (`cptcode`), CVX (`cvxcode`), NDC (`ndc`), RxNorm (`rxnorm`), LOINC (`loinc`), and NPI (`npi`). This means the data is coded, not just free text.\n- **Relationships via IDs**: Records are linked via IDs (`patientid`, `encounterid`, `transactionid`, `medicationid`, etc.), allowing reconstruction of relationships.\n- **Per-patient export**: The export is patient-scoped — each export file is for a single patient chart.\n- **Password protection**: The ZIP uses the patient DOB as password, which is a minimal security measure.\n\nA third party could reconstruct the clinical record from this export, though they would need to understand MicroMD's data model to interpret all the fields — many field names are self-explanatory (e.g., `firstname`, `icdcode`, `doseamount`) but some require domain knowledge (e.g., `gcnseqno`, `ADPType`, `bdagetype`).\n\n### Documentation Quality\n\n**Strengths:**\n- The document provides the **complete XML schema** for every export file, listing every element and attribute\n- The hierarchical nesting is clear\n- The format is self-documenting in that most attribute names are descriptive\n- The document is well-organized by file, with each XML file getting its own section\n- Recently updated (February 2026), suggesting active maintenance\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n- **No field-level descriptions**: Attributes are listed but never defined. What does `confidentiality` mean? What values can `billingstatus` take? What's the format of date fields?\n- **No data type specifications**: No indication of which fields are dates, integers, strings, coded values, etc.\n- **No value sets**: Coded fields like `maritalstatus`, `billingstatus`, `encountertype` lack enumeration of valid values\n- **No cardinality**: No indication of which elements can repeat or are required vs. optional\n- **No sample data**: No example export files or records showing what populated data looks like\n- **No import instructions**: A developer receiving this export would have to reverse-engineer the data types and value sets\n- **User manual referenced but not provided**: The document says \"see user manual for instruction\" on how to perform the export, but the manual is not publicly available\n- **No versioning information**: No indication of schema version or change history\n\n### Structure & Completeness\n\nThe documentation operates at the **attribute-name level** — it tells you exactly what fields exist in each XML element, which is more granular than just listing table names, but less granular than a full data dictionary with types, constraints, and descriptions. It is essentially an XML Schema rendered as prose, but without the formal type information that an actual XSD would provide.\n\nThe export is clearly the result of genuine (b)(10) work, not a repackaged (g)(10) FHIR API. It exports the full breadth of MicroMD's data model — billing, specialty workflows, OB/GYN, scheduling, DMS attachments — well beyond what any FHIR US Core API would cover. The proprietary XML format is appropriate for this purpose.\n\nThe critical gap is the lack of field-level documentation. A recipient of this export would know the structure but would need to guess at data types, valid values, and the meaning of ambiguous field names. Adding an actual XSD and a field glossary would significantly improve the documentation.\n\n## Access Summary\n- Final URL (after redirects): https://www.micromd.com/micromd-emr-certified/\n- Status: found\n- Required browser: no\n- Navigation complexity: one_click (single PDF link on certification page)\n- Anti-bot issues: none\n\n## Obstacles & Dead Ends\n- No obstacles encountered.
